<Text>Java Lanes was taken over by Kendall and Nicole Matheisen about a year or so ago from Bev and Jerry Martini, who decided to retire and take some much deserved time for themselves and family.  I am happy to say that Kendall and Nicole are doing an excellent job of carrying on the tradition started by the Martini's of providing an excellent wholesome place that any member of the family can enjoy.  You don't have to be a bowler to enjoy the sense of community provided by the people of Java Lanes, everyone welcomes you, first-time visitor, regular customer or even just the occasional drop in.  They are all family and everyone is welcome.  Of course, the food is great and the menu has been expanded to include many things that were not previously offered.  I go there myself several times during the week to watch the grandkids bowl, one of which is now bowling as an adult and to have lunch or even dinner with friends..............The service is excellent, and if you wish, there is also a bar available...........service there is top rate as well...........I would have to say that Java Lanes and the folks of Java Lanes are the catalyst that make our small community of Corning the family friendly place that it is.</Text><pictures>None<//pictures><Resp>None< /Resp><gmap_id>0x8082f2be4bad55ef:0x733cce02e6bc89e3</gmap_id></record>

I've been having trouble starting my truck recently, 3 times in the last week. I'm thinking that the problem is the corroded battery post connections. I stop by the nearest O'Reilly store to buy 2 new battery post connectors. The O'Reilly employee greets me and offers his assistance. I explained to him my problem. He takes me to the area in the store that has the new post connectiors. While I'm deciding which connectors to get he explains to me that he can check the battery, the starter, the alternator, all at no charge to me. I say 'Sounds good. Lets check it out'. The O'Reilly guy checks the alternator and it's good, no charge. Then he checks the starter and its good, no charge. Then he checks the battery and it's sbowing signs of failure, no charge. Then he gave me a written quote for 4 different batteries. Still.....NO CHARGE! WOW, that's what I call great customer service......and I hadn't even bought anything!</Review>

< review>
My driver's side electronic access(works off of body capacitance) door handle on my 2015 F150 Lariat started failing as the warranty was about to expire. Even the remote button on my key ring stopped working. Another one was ordered which comes with a back plate on the handle that requires painting. It was sent to the body shop for painting and then installed on my truck. It not only didn't get completely painted (some primer was still showing at the pivot point of the handle), but the body shop also sprayed right over dirt that was on the back plate. It looked bad. The body shop should not have considered it acceptable, Auburn Ford should not have accepted it when they picked it up and the mechanic that installed it should not of installed such a poorly painted back plate.
It required Ford taking my truck for another 3 days to correct the poor paint job on the back plate (I got a rental which Ford paid for). The paint job is still not as good as the the back plates of the handles that came from the factory on the other doors.
I think it would have very possible that Ford factory designed the back plate on the handle to be able to be removed from the original handle and installed on the replacement handle thus not requiring a few days at the body shop for painting.
Either way, good quality control keeps customers happier, repair costs down and was over looked no less than 4 times by the time I picked my truck up the first time. Incidentally (or not so), this is the 5th new Ford truck or van I have purchased since 1998.< /review>

<username>ed Farmer<//username><Time>1535782855332< /Time><Rate>1<//Rate><Review>BEWARE!!!  This place is a RIPOFF!  I bought a new Ford reman engine for my truck from Auburn Ford.  After the install, I had an engine code that would not go away.  I took it into the service department for their diagnosis.  I was told that the fuel pickup / sender and the fuel pump would need to be replaced (these parts are not covered under the engine warranty).  The cost for the repair would be almost $1900.  I had consulted with the mechanic and told him that i had just removed the fuel tank pickup, disassembled it and cleaned the filters and that the fuel pump was replaces just last year.  I am a professional mechanic and performed these procedures.  After my own further inspection I had found that the fuel pressure was very low and was the possible cause of the engine code.  I went ahead and replaced the fuel pump again with a factory unit per their recommendation.  Still low fuel pressure.  Upon my further inspection I located the fuel pressure regulator and disassembled it.  I took the fuel pressure regulator spring  and stretched it out from 1 1/4 in. to 1 5/8 in. and reinstalled.  The fuel pressure instantly went from 30 psi at idle (previously causing the engine code) to 60 psi at idle (much closer to where it should be). After a test drive, the engine code never returned.  This spring was a part of the new replacement engine I had just installed. The repair that was recommended by this shop would never have solved this problem.  I replaced the fuel pressure regulator spring (cost was $24.95) with a new one and the truck runs great.  Not only was this problem misdiagnosed  but I was charged $147 for it!  I also replaced the fuel pump that was not at all defective and that was $455.  I took my own time to solve the issue that should have been covered under warranty.
